  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_173ab710-d7b6-4c77-aeb8-00e68d9380eb'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();

  <span id="freeText17897601039432806615" style="display:none">The city of Canluum lies close to the scarred and desolate wastes of the Blight, a walled haven from the dangers away to the north, and a refuge from the ill works of those who serve the Dark One. Or so it is said.<br /><br />The city that greets Al’Lan Mandragoran, exiled king of Malkier and the finest swordsman of his generation, is instead one that is rife with rumour and the whisperings of Shadowspawn. Proof, should he have required it, that the Dark One grows powerful once more and that his minions are at work throughout the lands.<br /><br />And yet it is within Canluum’s walls that Lan will meet a woman who will shape his destiny. Moiraine is a young and powerful Aes Sedai who has journeyed to the city in search of a bondsman. She requires aid in a desperate quest to prove the truth of a vague and largely discredited prophecy—one that speaks of a means to turn back the shadow, and of a child who may be the dragon reborn.</span>

<div class='communityQuestionSubTitle'>
Popular Answered Questions

<div id='communityQuestionsWithAnswers'>
<div class='communityQuestionAndAnswer'>
<div class='communityQuestion'>
<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/594190-should-this-be-the-first-i-read-out-of-the">Should this be the first I read out of the wheel of time series? I see there is a book #1 and this is book #0 and was written after. I would like thoughts from people who read this series. Thanks.</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_594190'><a id="like_count_community_question_594190" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/594190?resource_type=CommunityQuestion"><span class="likesCount">5 likes</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F187065.New_Spring">like</a></span>

</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionTimestamp'>
<a href="/questions/594190-should-this-be-the-first-i-read-out-of-the">5 years ago</a>
</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionPermalink'>
<a href="/questions/594190-should-this-be-the-first-i-read-out-of-the">See all 11 answers</a>
</li>
</ul>
</div>

</div>
<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/9700268-tracy"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1337705898i/9700268._UY100_CR16,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/9700268-tracy">Tracy</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Not that you haven't already read what you will read, but should others wonder the same, I'd emphatically state that no, you should not.<br/><br/>One of the mai<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Not that you haven't already read what you will read, but should others wonder the same, I'd emphatically state that no, you should not.<br /><br />One of the main charms of The Wheel of Time is the mystery, unknowns and half-truths and questions. If you have read this story, you no longer have the ambiguity of feeling towards a few of the main characters. Your doubts are silenced. You read with frustration rather than fear and anxiety, and begin the books not as a confused youth following others into danger, but as a wise looker-on. Where is the fun?<br /><br />Additionally, this book has about 1/5 the pace of the first couple WoT novels. The initial pacing is intoxicating and pulls you through many duller volumes. This book is not a headlong flight into confusion, but more a detailed snapshot of a small moment that you only come to care deeply about once invested in the characters. Furthermore, the structure of the book is weak. One character is introduced and then disappears for half of the book, before all of the characters are finally united. <br /><br />I enjoyed it, but only because I had read the others before it.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerFooter'>

<div class='communityQuestionAndAnswer'>
<div class='communityQuestion'>
<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/1634418-does-the-book--series-have-simple">Does the book- series have simple languange-vocabulary? I&#39;m planning on reading it in english although it&#39;s not my native language.</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_1634418'><a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F187065.New_Spring">like</a></span>

</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionTimestamp'>
<a href="/questions/1634418-does-the-book--series-have-simple">one year ago</a>
</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionPermalink'>
<a href="/questions/1634418-does-the-book--series-have-simple">Add your answer</a>
</li>
</ul>
</div>

</div>
<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/21512558-su"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1372106875i/21512558.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/21512558-su">Su</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">It has fairly simple language complicated by the fact that there are constant references to Old Tongue sayings/terms and also catchphrases/terms from <a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">It has fairly simple language complicated by the fact that there are constant references to Old Tongue sayings/terms and also catchphrases/terms from every language and culture in the world, and there are quite a few, and some have their own old phrases which may be corruptions of other languages or old tongue words. Much like english has stolen and corrupted words form every other language.<br /><br />The beginning reader will soon be buried under cryptic references like Daes Dae'mar, Dai Shan, Aes Sedai, gaidin, saidar, saidin, Tel’aran’rhiod, aiel, da’covale, a'dam, etc etc. And there are hundreds like this.<br /><br />It's quite like how educated people of the 18th-19th century were fluent in multiple continental languages and interspersed their writing with latin, greek, french, german and italian words or quotes from classic writers in those languages.<br /><br />Each term is introduced and explained in the text but a glossary is required and included in the first book. You might also need an online resource, but be careful of spoilers if your eyes wander!<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://wot.fandom.com/wiki/The_Eye_of_the_World/Glossary">https://wot.fandom.com/wiki/The_Eye_o...</a><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.tor.com/2016/12/20/the-wheel-of-time-english-to-old-tongue-dictionary/">https://www.tor.com/2016/12/20/the-wh...</a> (can be used in reverse)<br /><br />Think of it a little like the secret language of Potterverse/Wizarding World fans, but amped up quite a bit so it's some work to learn them. That said the terms are unique to this world and once you do learn them you'll soon be sorting your <i>ter'angreals</i> from your <i>angreals</i> from your <i>sa'angreals</i> as you contemplate <i>toh</i> using <i>ko'di</i>. :)<br /><br />Edit: Spelling and clarification<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerFooter'>

<div id="review_404374100" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/404374100" />
    <a title="Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10336538-jessica-silverbow"><img alt="Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1393785730p2/10336538.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/404374100?book_show_action=true">Aug 31, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ " href="/user/show/10336538-jessica-silverbow">Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/8892653-new-spring">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=favorite-secondary-characters">favorite-secondary-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=not-your-ordinary-creatures">not-your-ordinary-creatures</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=rabid-reads-reviews">rabid-reads-reviews</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=i-hate-this-heroine">i-hate-this-heroine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=i-have-rules">i-have-rules</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=i-am-so-bored">i-am-so-bored</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=the-book-boy-is-mine">the-book-boy-is-mine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=cover-whore">cover-whore</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=best-series">best-series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer404374100" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15927044976802142692"><b>Reviewed by: <a href='http://rabidreads.ca/2016/11/review-new-spring-by-robert-jordan.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>Rabid Reads</a></b><br/><br/>This book gave me FEELINGS . . . <br/><br/>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1416451466ra/11968918.gif' width='400' height='225' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
<br/><br/> . . . few of them good.<br/><br/>For the first time in a WoT reread, I found myself absolutely hating the content. <br/><br/>HATING. <br/><br/>The only reason NEW SPRING didn't get one-starred is b/c there are more than a few poignant Lan moments. But without those . . . *flares nostrils*<br/><br/>The first problem is that the front half to two-thirds of the book is slow as molasses. <br/><br/>Noooooothiiiiiing haaaaaappennnnns. <br/><br/>Well, okay, <i>something</i> happens--Gitara, the same Aes Sed</span>
  <span id="freeText15927044976802142692" style="display:none"><b>Reviewed by: <a href="http://rabidreads.ca/2016/11/review-new-spring-by-robert-jordan.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Rabid Reads</a></b><br><br>This book gave me FEELINGS . . . <br><br>
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1416451466ra/11968918.gif" width="400" height="225" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
<br><br> . . . few of them good.<br><br>For the first time in a WoT reread, I found myself absolutely hating the content. <br><br>HATING. <br><br>The only reason NEW SPRING didn't get one-starred is b/c there are more than a few poignant Lan moments. But without those . . . *flares nostrils*<br><br>The first problem is that the front half to two-thirds of the book is slow as molasses. <br><br>Noooooothiiiiiing haaaaaappennnnns. <br><br>Well, okay, <i>something</i> happens--Gitara, the same Aes Sedai who sent Tigraine to the Waste, foretells the Dragon's rebirth then falls over dead, while Siuan and Moiraine are in attendance--<i>then</i> nothing happens. <br><br>They spend a bunch of time in Tar Valon, first doing clerical work, then forced into projects by higher-ranking Aes Sedai, and it's 60% before Moiraine gets around to fleeing the Tower, but she's so awful that I almost wished we were back in the Tower doing nothing. <br><br><b>You:</b> How awful was she?<br><br><b>Me:</b> Do you remember how bad she was the first few books? How manipulative? How superior?<br><br><b>You:</b> Yes . . . <br><br><b>Me:</b> That x100.<br><br><b>You:</b> O_____O<br><br><b>Me:</b> EXACTLY. *fumes*<br><br>Any temperance she'd learned, any restraint, is G-O-N-E. Combine that with her dual sense of entitlement (newly raised Sister + Cairhienin nobility) and you've got yourself a Moiraine. *throws her back*<br><br>She tortures Lan--premeditatedly and on a nightly basis--b/c not realizing he was in the company of an Aes Sedai, he said to a friend (while she eavesdropped) that he'd prefer to avoid their company. She abuses stray animals with flicks of the Power, and she leaves a shady innkeeper to be gang-raped, b/c it's no less than the woman deserves (according to Herself).<br><br>So yeah . . . Moiraine is vile.<br><br>Then there's the Lady Edeyn, also known as Lan's <i>carneira</i>. <br><br>"What's a <i>carneira</i>?" you ask, and that's an excellent question. It's a man<s>boy</s>'s first lover, but it's ever so much more complicated than that. <br><br>In Malkier, men don't approach women to show their interest. Women do the chasing. But b/c of the constraints on male behavior (b/c courtesy), it'd be pretty tricky for a man to spurn the advances of a woman he isn't interested in without causing offense.<br><br>So that's obnoxious.<br><br>Enter Lady Edeyn, the 30+-year-old woman who seduced Lan at the tender age of . . . wait for it . . . FIFTEEN.<br><br>
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1478682202ra/21099028.gif" width="245" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
<br><br>And if you think that's bad, you'd better hold onto your hat, b/c this bitch wants Lan to marry HER DAUGHTER. <br><br>YEP.<br><br>Ask me when she informs him of her little plan. Go ahead. Ask me.<br><br><b>You:</b> ???<br><br>When she's manipulating him back into bed with her.<br><br>YES. That's right. You didn't misread or misunderstand.<br><br>
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1478682517ra/21099057.gif" width="500" height="252" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
<br><br>I could continue to rant, but really? What's the point? Yeah, Siuan being a featherbrain and painting a red, flashing target over her head for the Black Ajah to see was aggravating, but it can't compete with the misdeeds of others, so why bother? <br><br>Suffice it to say that I do NOT recommend NEW SPRING, in fact, I so absolutely <i>do not</i> recommend it that my recommendation is to skip it entirely. You don't learn anything necessary to the continuation of the series, so do yourself a favor and toss this one on the burn pile. #goodriddance.<br><br><b>NOTICE:</b> this reread is in preparation for finally biting the bullet and reading book 14. That means I HAVE NOT read book 14 yet. Please be mindful of this in the comments, both for me and for others who may or may not have progressed past this point in the series. Thank you.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1421060968i/13316940.jpg" alt="Jessica Signature" width="205" height="101" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>My other reviews for this series:</b><br><br><b>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/705725321" rel="nofollow noopener">The Eye of the World (Wheel of Time, #1) by Robert Jordan</a>
</b><br><b>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/404373567" rel="nofollow noopener">The Great Hunt (Wheel of Time, #2) by Robert Jordan</a>
</b><br><b>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/351590687" rel="nofollow noopener">The Dragon Reborn (Wheel of Time, #3) by Robert Jordan</a>

<div id="review_1796582205" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1796582205" />
    <a title="Robin (Bridge Four)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14105531-robin-bridge-four"><img alt="Robin (Bridge Four)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1473392517p2/14105531.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1796582205?book_show_action=true">Nov 08, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Robin (Bridge Four)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Robin (Bridge Four)" href="/user/show/14105531-robin-bridge-four">Robin (Bridge Four)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=awesome-audio">awesome-audio</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=want-to-throw-across-the-room">want-to-throw-across-the-room</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=beautifully-broken-bastards">beautifully-broken-bastards</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1796582205" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15655831465512749652"><b>1.5 I’m Sorry To Do This Stars</b><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1464670462ra/19261874.gif' width='400' height='267' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Okay hear me out….I totally admit the Robert Jordan has a fantastic and complex world full of intricately detailed world building with cultures, religions and landscaping. But if it takes 60% for your books to go anywhere and you destroy beloved characters along the way I’m totally going to have a problem.<br/><br/>So this is supposed to be an origin story or a prequel to the Wheel of Time series set a little less than 20 years before Eye of the World. The problem with preque</span>
  <span id="freeText15655831465512749652" style="display:none"><b>1.5 I’m Sorry To Do This Stars</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1464670462ra/19261874.gif" width="400" height="267" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Okay hear me out….I totally admit the Robert Jordan has a fantastic and complex world full of intricately detailed world building with cultures, religions and landscaping. But if it takes 60% for your books to go anywhere and you destroy beloved characters along the way I’m totally going to have a problem.<br><br>So this is supposed to be an origin story or a prequel to the Wheel of Time series set a little less than 20 years before Eye of the World. The problem with prequels in general is that they are really hard to pull off and make interesting because you know where the story is going to go. I think the only author I’ve read to do it and do it well is <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/2063919.Michael_J__Sullivan" title="Michael J. Sullivan" rel="nofollow noopener">Michael J. Sullivan</a> with the Riyria Chronicles. It is really hard to build enough tension for the story to make it great <b>and that is PROBLEM #1 </b><br><br>So moving onto <b>Problem #2 taking forever to do anything</b>. This starts out decent with the foreseeing that ‘The Dragon is Born’ and the events that started Siuan and Moriane on their lifetime journey to find him. But then….nothing really happens for 150 more pages. I mean things sort of happen. We get another in-depth look into the daily life of an Aes Sedea and it makes me like them even less. Really does every woman in this series have to be a ninny, spoiled brat, bitch or trying to one up another woman??? But the story doesn’t begin to take off until Moriane leaves the tower around 60%. That is a lot of time plotting and maneuvering without ever doing anything. The only thing that I appreciated in this first half of the book is FINALLY seeing what the test to become a full sister looked like.<br><br><b>Problem #3 was thinking of characters one way and then seeing them another.</b> I loved both Lan and Moraine from the series. I mean 10 books in and I’m a little attached to the way I see the characters from then. So to go back to 16 years ago to see how Moraine behaved then, OMG she was awful…totally and completely awful. I’m not even talking about the way she treated Lan to get back at a perceived slight by him….which was completely childish and reminded me more of Elayne the daughter Heir’s haughty behavior. No not just that but she <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[swatted a dog (a non-menacing dog) out of the way with the one power because it barked at her when she came into town. She was in a very bad part of town and woman tried to drug her. It is thought that she would be used or sold into a brothel after that. So she makes the woman who was going to give it to her drink it instead. Moraine then leaves said woman there to be gang raped. GANG RAPED!!! She doesn’t know anything about the woman or how she was pressed into this service or if she was the one that had the idea to do it for her own profit.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Moraine is of the Blue Ajah <b>who involve themselves with righteous causes and justice.</b> Does that seem like justice to you??? It sure didn’t to me and I was not okay with it.<br><br><b>By the end I hated her and all her proclamations that she would bring Lan to heel.</b> I was hoping he’d drop her in another lake and wander the road alone.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1399251886ra/9526544.gif" width="400" height="226" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Moving on….<b>PROBLEM #4</b>I’m going to say something I really thought I’d never say. I don’t want to read another relationship coupling written by Robert Jordan EVER. The pairings in this book are so weird and uncomfortable. The one involving Lan <b>SO AKWARD and EWEEEEE</b>. No really between Mat and Tylin, Rand and Elayne <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[while the other women and Birgetta could feel what was going on <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, Lan and <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Myrelle (even though we never see it. It is known that is how she liked to bring warders back from the death of their Aes Sedae) <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. Some of the Forsaken and their playthings along with now Lan and Edeyn. <br><br>Edeyn was over thirty when Lan was fifteen and she took his virginity to be able to control many of his actions for life. This is where it gets icky…even more icky than that first sentence <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[she uses that tradition as a way to make him marry her daughter. Even as she is taking him to bed again…because apparently since she was his first lover she has that power over him she is telling him he will marry her daughter. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> *<b>I just threw up little in my mouth</b>*<br><br>I honestly hated that was in this book. I didn’t like being involved in yet another weird power heavy sex thing due to custom. It is even more akward because you know who he ends up with later. I didn’t want to know he had sex with yet another woman in his past. I normally like knowing a few of the characters in my fantasy are having sex. But Jordan seems to make it really strange, akward and weird and I want no part of it anymore.<br><br><b>The only thing that went right</b>. Well this is Robert Jordan so you know that just about everything is going to happen in the last 15%. That is totally true here and the confrontation with the Black Ajah and the plots they hatched were the best aspect to this story. So I will say that the action in the end saved the story a little for me. Also if this wasn’t a prequel I would have been maybe rooting for relationship between Siuan and Moraine but since I’m firmly solidified in wanting those two with other people later in the series I couldn’t put much interest behind that either.<br><br><b>Suggestions</b> If you aren’t that far into the series and really attached to a few of the characters then this is maybe a good thing to read for a little Aes Sedea back story and a little more depth to Lan’s character. If you just LOVE all things Robert Jordan then it also probably won’t be an issue for you. But if like me you have firm attachments to who people are and you didn’t like the Mat/Tylin seduction then this is probably not for you.<br></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="15655831465512749652" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1796435862" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7272616844700394611">This WoT prequel is the story of how Moiraine and Lan first met and of how Moiraine and Siuan got caught up in all the Dragon Reborn related intrigue. It is set 20 years before the happenings in Eye of the World. <br/><br/>The story was actually better than I was expecting it to be. It was told mostly from Moiraine's POV, but we also got a number of chapters from Lan's POV. It gave both characters plenty of time to shine and I definitely like both of them a lot more after reading their adventures in this </span>
  <span id="freeText7272616844700394611" style="display:none">This WoT prequel is the story of how Moiraine and Lan first met and of how Moiraine and Siuan got caught up in all the Dragon Reborn related intrigue. It is set 20 years before the happenings in Eye of the World. <br /><br />The story was actually better than I was expecting it to be. It was told mostly from Moiraine's POV, but we also got a number of chapters from Lan's POV. It gave both characters plenty of time to shine and I definitely like both of them a lot more after reading their adventures in this story. <br /><br />An added plus was the fact that we got to see all sorts of familiar characters in their younger days. It is fun to see how some have changed over the years and how some have not! <br /><br />All in all I thought this sequel was a worthy addition the the WoT series. It is just a pity that Jordan never got the chance to write the second and third prequel books he had planned before he died. <br /><br />Rating: 4 stars.<br /><br />Audio Note: As always Reading and Krammer did a great job! <br /></span>

<div id="review_381065389" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/381065389" />
    <a title="Evgeny" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9340136-evgeny"><img alt="Evgeny" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1544797852p2/9340136.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/381065389?book_show_action=true">Jul 31, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Evgeny" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Evgeny" href="/user/show/9340136-evgeny">Evgeny</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/8892653-new-spring">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9340136-evgeny?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer381065389" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12905139233330628197">The plot of this book can be summarized in the following two sentences. Moiraine and Siuan Sanche learn a great secret while still being Accepted in the White Tower. Moiraine meets Lan. There are much more than these events in the prequel and some more familiar faces appear than the ones I already mentioned.<br/><br/>I gave this book 5 stars initially, but I was sure I would lower the rating to 4 stars after I read this tale for the second time. To my complete surprise I realized that is still worth 5 sta</span>
  <span id="freeText12905139233330628197" style="display:none">The plot of this book can be summarized in the following two sentences. Moiraine and Siuan Sanche learn a great secret while still being Accepted in the White Tower. Moiraine meets Lan. There are much more than these events in the prequel and some more familiar faces appear than the ones I already mentioned.<br /><br />I gave this book 5 stars initially, but I was sure I would lower the rating to 4 stars after I read this tale for the second time. To my complete surprise I realized that is still worth 5 stars. I think the good prequels must show how some of the relationship already developed in the main storyline came to be and some insights on their development. In this regard the book succeeds - no questions about it. It also happened to have interesting and fast-moving (in the second half of the book) plot.<br /><br />The first half of the book is mostly spent on Moiraine and Siuan Sanche training in the White Tower. While this part is somewhat slower, I still find it interesting. I always wondered what the test for full Aes Sedai looks like: we are shown test for Accepted from both Nynaeve and Egwene POV, but never the former. This book gives Moiraine's POV during this test as well as preparation for it.<br /><br />Robert Jordan once again showed his strength as a worldbuilder: he gave interesting glimpses of Malkieri culture: original and unique; in the first ten books Lan was the only Malkieri we get to see.<br /><br />The prequel totally deserves 5 stars as it completely fulfills its purpose while being interesting. One last piece of advice: the book contains minor spoilers; it is better to read it in publication order (after book 10). <br /><br />This review is a copy/paste of my BookLikes one: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://gene.booklikes.com/post/814562/surprisingly-this-prequel-is-not-useless">http://gene.booklikes.com/post/814562...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="12905139233330628197" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Phrynne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8655084-phrynne"><img alt="Phrynne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577753809p2/8655084.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1370387390?book_show_action=true">Aug 21, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1370387390" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15042802760931017834">I have read and loved the entire Wheel of Time series so it was fun to read the prequel to the whole affair. I really enjoyed finding out how Moiraine and Lan met and how he became her warder. I also liked all the information about the White Tower and the Aes Sedai. There is nothing in this book that you have to know before enjoying the rest of the series but it is a nice little piece of background information. Loved the ending - it almost made me go and pick up Book 1 to read again. </span>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_35258316" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/35258316" />
    <a title="Ryan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1500718-ryan"><img alt="Ryan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1238846167p2/1500718.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/35258316?book_show_action=true">Oct 14, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ryan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ryan" href="/user/show/1500718-ryan">Ryan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer35258316" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3584733196713266282">Sometimes I feel like reading fantasy is just a waste of time. If nothing else, the themes are often distressingly adolescent and no matter how many times I read about slaying dragons, it's pretty unlikely that I'll ever slay a dragon in real life.<br/><br/>Perhaps, for me, the real attraction that sword & sorcery offers is an escape into a world of imagination. It sounds like a corny movie trailer (I'm sure everyone can hear the movie trailer voice when reading "esCApe... into a worlld ... of imagiNAtion</span>
  <span id="freeText3584733196713266282" style="display:none">Sometimes I feel like reading fantasy is just a waste of time. If nothing else, the themes are often distressingly adolescent and no matter how many times I read about slaying dragons, it's pretty unlikely that I'll ever slay a dragon in real life.<br /><br />Perhaps, for me, the real attraction that sword &amp; sorcery offers is an escape into a world of imagination. It sounds like a corny movie trailer (I'm sure everyone can hear the movie trailer voice when reading "esCApe... into a worlld ... of imagiNAtion"), but I guess it's true.<br /><br />Some fantasy authors manage to create amazing atmospheres without the encyclopedia details -- China Mieville's "Bas Lag" books and Gene Wolfe's "Solar Cycle" come to mind. Others take the encyclopedia route.<br /><br />Of the encyclopediasts, one of my favorites is Robert Jordan.<br /><br />Say what you like about Jordan's writing -- seriously, go ahead -- "The Wheel of Time" series stands out for its highly detailed world building.<br /><br />And <i>New Spring</i> does a fine job of representing Jordan's world-building skills.<br /><br />Published after <i>Path of Daggers</i> (book 8), <i>New Spring</i> is a prequel (Book 0) to the regular series. None of the major protagonists -- not Rand, not Mat, not Perrin, not Elayne, not Nynaeve, not Egwene, not Faile, not Loial, not Ishmael, not Min -- are present. Instead, Jordan tells the story of how Moiraine met Lan -- if you're thinking <i>When Harry Met Sally</i>, you're way off.<br /><br />It seems that the Black Ajah has begun hunting for the Dragon Reborn. Will Moiraine beat them to the finish line?<br /><br /><i>New Spring</i> is an enjoyable entry in "The Wheel of Time," and I don't think it's the uncertainty Moiraine feels as she tries to impress her peers or Lan fighting off six (count'em, six!) swordsman that makes this entry stand out. Rather, it's the world that Jordan created that allows this novella to "capture our imagination."<br /><br />After all, <i>New Spring</i> was published at a time when "The Wheel of Time" had become almost hopelessly bogged down in ongoing ... ongoing ... plots and a phone book's worth of supporting characters. Freed of all this baggage, <i>New Spring</i> makes the WOT feel fun again.<br /><br />I once read that Jordan had begun to make plans for a second fantasy series after he'd finished with the "Wheel of Time", and it's quite saddening that he passed away before he was able to start it. I sometimes wonder if he resented having to finish "The Wheel of Time" before he could move on to a new world.<br /><br />Regardless, Jordan's writing may suffer from any number of obsessive writing disorders, but when I'm stuck in traffic, I am grateful that I've taken the time to read fantasy, and "The Wheel of Time."</span>
  <a data-text-id="3584733196713266282" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_823255307" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/823255307" />

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Claudia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Claudia" href="/user/show/20498957-claudia">Claudia</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

            Shelves:

              <span id="reviewTextContainer823255307" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer11895402428908409710"><b>2nd read</b><br/><br/>Four years ago, I fell in love with <i>Wheel of Time</i> and read all 15 volumes in less than three months. To this day, it’s still my number One series.<br/><br/>Some say this prequel should be read in publication order, as it was written after <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/113435.Crossroads_of_Twilight__Wheel_of_Time___10_' title='Crossroads of Twilight (Wheel of Time, #10) by Robert Jordan' rel='nofollow noopener'>Crossroads of Twilight</a>, which is the 10th. Well, I started with it and it helped a lot with the intricacies of Aes Sedai schemes and the relationship between some of its main characters; it also sheds light on the Foretelling of the Dragon Reborn. But if you want</span>
  <span id="freeText11895402428908409710" style="display:none"><b>2nd read</b><br><br>Four years ago, I fell in love with <i>Wheel of Time</i> and read all 15 volumes in less than three months. To this day, it’s still my number One series.<br><br>Some say this prequel should be read in publication order, as it was written after <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/113435.Crossroads_of_Twilight__Wheel_of_Time___10_" title="Crossroads of Twilight (Wheel of Time, #10) by Robert Jordan" rel="nofollow noopener">Crossroads of Twilight</a>, which is the 10th. Well, I started with it and it helped a lot with the intricacies of Aes Sedai schemes and the relationship between some of its main characters; it also sheds light on the Foretelling of the Dragon Reborn. But if you want to discover everything on the go, you may read it whenever pleases you, as it takes place about 20-30 years before the start of events in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/228665.The_Eye_of_the_World__Wheel_of_Time___1_" title="The Eye of the World (Wheel of Time, #1) by Robert Jordan" rel="nofollow noopener">The Eye of the World</a>.<br><br>The volume is more explanatory than anything else: the focus is on Moiraine and Lan (two of the key characters in the books to come), how their paths crossed and clarifies the journey ahead with its ultimate goal. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1516816384i/24903760._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1516816384i/24903761.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Mind you, the series is not focused on action; it has its share of battles – some takes few hundred pages in the volumes to come – but mostly is a coming of age story, for more than one character. The world building is colossal– a lot of nations, each one with its specifics and myriad details about them –, the magic system is exquisite and there are twists upon twists, all these gradually revealed in the long journey. It has a lot of influences from Tolkien and various myths, but I think they are perfectly adapted for this universe. <br><br>First time I read it with a printed map near me and now I realized that I have memorized it and I know the location of each nation and every main town on it – that’s how much I immersed myself in it.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1516816384i/24903762.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Of course, it’s a matter of subjectivity, but I will always prefer this kind of fantasy, with a vast scope and epic journeys, strong worldbuilding and a magic system gradually revealed and not too wide-spread, instead of grim action-packed ones. If you want a comparison, Dragon Reborn’s and his companions' journey is quite similar in its ‘epicness’ with the one of Frodo’s, only more elaborate. In my opinion, it’s more like the movies than the books, due to the visual impact (I found LOTR books too telegraphic).<br><br>I could start it again tomorrow and I would enjoy it just as much, that’s how much I love it 😊<br>(21-24.01.2018)<br><br>----<br><br><b>1st read</b><br><br>If this, lets say, prelude made me give it 5 stars, I'm really anxious to see what's hidden in the next 14 volumes... <br>(14-18.11.2014)</span>

<div id="review_2818045310" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2818045310" />
    <a title="Zitong Ren" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/77983193-zitong-ren"><img alt="Zitong Ren" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1552188473p2/77983193.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2818045310?book_show_action=true">Jul 25, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Zitong Ren" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Zitong Ren" href="/user/show/77983193-zitong-ren">Zitong Ren</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780356504759" href="/book/show/25371657-new-spring">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/77983193-zitong-ren?shelf=action">action</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/77983193-zitong-ren?shelf=2020">2020</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/77983193-zitong-ren?shelf=epics">epics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/77983193-zitong-ren?shelf=adult">adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/77983193-zitong-ren?shelf=contains-romance">contains-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/77983193-zitong-ren?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/77983193-zitong-ren?shelf=adventure">adventure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/77983193-zitong-ren?shelf=diverse">diverse</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2818045310" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8583897141072429863">So, this was really nice. This was the first time that I read New Spring, which tells the story of Moiraine and Lan 20 years before the start of the main series. As much as I enjoyed this book, I am going to give it 4 stars and not 5, which is my usual ratings for most Wheel of Time books, largely based off personal enjoyment.<br/><br/>It was interesting reading this, as all the characters that we see in this compared to the main series are so different! Like totally different people, which was unexpected</span>
  <span id="freeText8583897141072429863" style="display:none">So, this was really nice. This was the first time that I read New Spring, which tells the story of Moiraine and Lan 20 years before the start of the main series. As much as I enjoyed this book, I am going to give it 4 stars and not 5, which is my usual ratings for most Wheel of Time books, largely based off personal enjoyment.<br /><br />It was interesting reading this, as all the characters that we see in this compared to the main series are so different! Like totally different people, which was unexpected off course, but normally when I read about Moiraine, Siuan or Lan, they are generally so composed and calm characters who are always in control and are largely confident of themselves. Then there is this book, where you have Moiraine and Siuan talking about boys and profusely blushing which was just so strange. Now, in the main series, there were still signs of the sort of character/person that they were before, where there is a scene in The Shadow Rising where Moiraine are chatting with Elayne, Nynaeve and Egwene and I found that to be interesting as it showed that Moiraine wasn’t always this super serious and focussed Aes Sedai. In this book, it was just so different and by the end of the novel, you do see her start to develop into the character that she does end up becoming.<br /><br />Now one of the best parts of this novel for me was definitely the relationship between Moiraine and Siuan and I actually really liked their chemistry together. Both of them are generally considered to be bi, though I don’t think there’s any real confirmation of that, but they are both queer at the very least. A great portion of the Wheel of Time was written before LGBTQIA+ characters did come to the forefront of fiction and it wasn’t something that was done often back in the those days(or largely accepted unfortunately) and I do appreciate it more that while there is no explicit content of the two, lots of things are certainly applied and to be fair to Jordan, that was probably as much as he was allowed when he was writing the Wheel of Time. <br /><br />Compared to the main novels, this is about maybe half the length, if even that of the books in the main series. Due to that, it was a lot more contained and largely took place in two main settings, instead of all over the continent, which worked really well for this. It also followed a much smaller cast of characters and was largely a much easier read compared to the main series. However, this is also where some of my criticisms come in. For the main series, I generally excuse the slow pacing and repetitive nature of most of the books as it is such a long series and the payoff, especially in the last few books is so worth it considering the amount of foreshadowing that there is and the worldbuilding is just absolutely top notch. Since this is a four-hundred-page novel however, I actually probably would have liked for there to be bit punchier and more exciting, and while I know that the second half of the book picks up considerable, it wasn’t by much. The first half of the book, aside from the Moiraine and Siuan being awesome characters, much of it was actually fairly boring. Yes, things happen, but considering that it is only four hundred novel, not enough consequential or important things occurred. <br /><br />Don’t get me wrong, I still really enjoyed this book, but it wasn’t quite good enough for it to be a five star despite how much I love the characters enjoy spending time in the world. Talking about the world, this book actually adds a lot of really nice lore and contextualises a fair number of things in the main series which was great and we really get to learn a fair bit about character back stories and also just being there for these events that we largely know about, but not to this level of detail.<br /><br />So, that’s review of New Spring, I hope it was ok. 8/10</span>
  <a data-text-id="8583897141072429863" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2366257" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2366257" />
    <a title="Nicole" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/136380-nicole"><img alt="Nicole" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1479497572p2/136380.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2366257?book_show_action=true">Jun 25, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nicole" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nicole" href="/user/show/136380-nicole">Nicole</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780765306296" href="/book/show/1001544.New_Spring">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">fantasy fiction lovers with stamina</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2366257" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9041242199609418648">I read the Wheel of Time series by Robert Jordan because both my husband and best friend had read them. The best friend highly encouraged me to read the books - my husband warned me off.<br/><br/>The warning is not because the books are bad. The first few, actually, are very good. Great character development, interesting universe for those who love fantasy novels.<br/><br/>The warning is because these books never, ever, ever are going to end. Ever.<br/><br/>There are so far 12 books (including a prequel that came out somewhe</span>
  <span id="freeText9041242199609418648" style="display:none">I read the Wheel of Time series by Robert Jordan because both my husband and best friend had read them. The best friend highly encouraged me to read the books - my husband warned me off.<br /><br />The warning is not because the books are bad. The first few, actually, are very good. Great character development, interesting universe for those who love fantasy novels.<br /><br />The warning is because these books never, ever, ever are going to end. Ever.<br /><br />There are so far 12 books (including a prequel that came out somewhere between books 10 and 11). Each book is close to 1000 pages. I think the last six books have taken place over the book plot timeline of about a month. Seriously. One or two books may have only covered a day or two. No lie.<br /><br />The books start off with just 4-5 main characters...but over time I think there become closer to 20. And everyone rates their own storyline. As the books stand now, I think almost everyone is in a completely different country on a different mission. It can get confusing for those not quite looking for that sort of depth.<br /><br />Nonetheless...once you get far enough in the series you'll keep going. If for no other reason than you feel obligated. At this point, all those of us who've kept us are just praying that Robert Jordan doesn't die before finishing the series because there are so many plot lines left untied. <br /><br />For those serious about fantasy fiction, these books are somewhat of a right of passage. A necessary evil.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9041242199609418648" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1466277827" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1466277827" />
    <a title="Sotiris Karaiskos" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18940246-sotiris-karaiskos"><img alt="Sotiris Karaiskos" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1407195235p2/18940246.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1466277827?book_show_action=true">Dec 11, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sotiris Karaiskos" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sotiris Karaiskos" href="/user/show/18940246-sotiris-karaiskos">Sotiris Karaiskos</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook " href="/book/show/12743291-new-spring">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18940246-sotiris-karaiskos?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18940246-sotiris-karaiskos?shelf=high-fantasy">high-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1466277827" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9755872940015245643">Moirane, Lan and Siuan are three of the most important characters in the whole of the Wheel of Time, but we mainly watch their course from a distance, with the writer very rarely giving us their own perspective and thus a closer look to their thoughts and to their feelings. This omission is somehow corrected by this book that is also taking us the beginning of the story.<br/><br/>There we meet Moiraine at an earlier age as an Accepted in the White Tower, shortly before gain the title of Aes Sedai, along w</span>
  <span id="freeText9755872940015245643" style="display:none">Moirane, Lan and Siuan are three of the most important characters in the whole of the Wheel of Time, but we mainly watch their course from a distance, with the writer very rarely giving us their own perspective and thus a closer look to their thoughts and to their feelings. This omission is somehow corrected by this book that is also taking us the beginning of the story.<br /><br />There we meet Moiraine at an earlier age as an Accepted in the White Tower, shortly before gain the title of Aes Sedai, along with her friend Siuan. Naturally, 20 years ago, her personality is completely different, she is more immature, more insecure, less serious, moody, emotionally weaker, yet having the same determination to do what she needs. Siuan has the same immaturity and insecurity, but the basic ingredients of her character were the same as in the main series. Their friendship in this first stage is very strong, with this emotional bonding being described to us in a very beautiful way by the writer. In the hard training they have to undergo, this friendship give them power that they need too much when they learn about the beginning of fulfilling the prophecy for the rebirth of the Dragon, and finally understand the important role they have to play. Through their experience in the White Tower we learn a lot of things about the conditions in which women are trained and the customs of the Aes Sedai, which of course makes this book even more interesting.<br /><br />On the other hand Lan, at this age, he is already the hard and serious warrior we know, the one who submits wholeheartedly to duty and sworn to die for it. The only difference he may have is perhaps more laxity, his distrust in Aes Sedai but also the forced engagement with the - pleasant - customs of his lost motherland. The latter also gives the writer the opportunity to bring us some of these customs and to talk to us about the rather relaxed sexual morals of Kandor. His encounter with Moirane is rather unexpected and at first their relationship does not seem to go so well but when the forces of the Dark One make their appearance and they give their first common battle against them they understand that they must ally themselves to help saving the world by finding the Dragon Reborn.<br /><br />Generally, a very interesting book, slightly different in style than the books of the main series, is filling some gaps, shows us some more aspects of this fantastic world and above all gives us the opportunity to follow in an interesting story some of our favorite heroes. As far as I know the author had the intention of writing a series of such smaller books that would show some other aspects of the story but unfortunately the illness prevented him and we were deprived of a series of such small masterpieces that would grow a bit more the epic scale of his work. The wheel, however, turns as it pleases and eventually allowed only that to became written, so let's read it and enjoy it without thinking about anything else.<br /><br />Η Moirane, ο Lan και η Siuan είναι τρία από τα πιο σημαντικά πρόσωπα σε ολόκληρη τη σειρά του Τροχού του Χρόνου, κυρίως, όμως, παρακολουθούμε την πορεία τους από απόσταση, με τον συγγραφέα πολύ σπάνια να μας δίνει τη δική τους οπτική γωνία και με αυτό το τρόπο μία κοντινότερη μάτια στις σκέψεις και στα συναισθήματά τους. Αυτήν την παράλειψη έρχεται να τη διορθώσει αυτό το βιβλίο, πηγαίνοντας μας παράλληλα στην αρχή της ιστορίας.<br /><br />Εκεί συναντάμε την Moirane σε νεαρή ηλικία να βρίσκεται ως αποδεκτή στο Λευκό Πύργο, λίγο πριν αποκτήσει τον τίτλο της Aes Sedai, μαζί με τη φίλη της τη Siuan. Φυσικά 20 χρόνια πριν είναι ένας άνθρωπος εντελώς διαφορετικός, πιο ανώριμη, πιο ανασφαλής, λιγότερο σοβαρή, με διάθεση για φάρσες, συναισθηματικά πιο αδύναμη, έχοντας, όμως, την ίδια αποφασιστικότητα για να κάνει αυτό που πρέπει. Έχει την ίδια ανωριμότητα και ανασφάλεια αλλά τα βασικά συστατικά του χαρακτήρα της ήταν ίδια με αυτά που δείχνει στην κυρία σειρά. Η φιλία τους σε αυτό το πρώτο στάδιο είναι πολύ ισχυρή, με αυτό το συναισθηματικό δέσιμο να μεταφέρεται με πολύ όμορφο τρόπο από το συγγραφέα. Μέσα στη σκληρή εκπαίδευση που πρέπει να υποστούν τους δίνει δύναμη που τη χρειάζονται πάρα πολύ όταν μαθαίνουν για την αρχή της εκπλήρωσης της προφητείας για τη γέννηση του Δράκου και καταλαβαίνουν τελικά τον σημαντικό ρόλο που πρέπει να παίξουν. Μέσα από αυτή την πορεία τους στο Λευκό Πύργο μαθαίνουμε αρκετά πράγματα για τις συνθήκες στις οποίες εκπαιδεύονται οι μαθητευόμενες και τα έθιμα των Aes Sedai, κάτι που φυσικά κάνει αυτό το βιβλίο ακόμα πιο ενδιαφέρον.<br /><br />Από την άλλη ο σε αυτήν την ηλικία είναι ήδη ο σκληρός και σοβαρός πολεμιστής που γνωρίζουμε, ο υποταγμένος ολόψυχα στο καθήκον και ορκισμένος να πεθάνει για αυτό. Το μόνο διαφορετικό που έχει είναι ίσως μία περισσότερη χαλαρότητα, η δυσπιστία του απέναντι στις Aes Sedai αλλά και η αναγκαστική ενασχόληση με τα - ευχάριστα - έθιμα της χαμένης του πατρίδας. Το τελευταίο δίνει και μία αφορμή στον συγγραφέα να μας μεταφέρει μερικά αυτά τα έθιμα και να μας μιλήσει για τα μάλλον κάπως χαλαρά ήθη του Kandor. Η συνάντηση του με την Moiraine είναι μάλλον απρόσμενη και στην αρχή δεν φαίνεται να τα πηγαίνουν και τόσο καλά, όταν, όμως, οι δυνάμεις του Σκοτεινού κάνουν την εμφάνιση τους και δίνουν την πρώτη κοινή τους μάχη εναντίον τους καταλαβαίνουν ότι πρέπει να συμμαχήσουν για να βοηθήσουν στη σωτηρία του κόσμου βρίσκοντας τον Αναγεννημένο Δράκοντα.<br /><br />Γενικά ένα πολύ ενδιαφέρον βιβλίο, λίγο διαφορετικό σε ύφος από αυτά της κύριας σειράς, που γεμίζει κάποια κενά, μας δείχνει μερικές ακόμα πτυχές αυτού του φανταστικού κόσμου και πάνω από όλα μας δίνει την ευκαιρία να ακολουθήσουμε σε μία ενδιαφέρουσα ιστορία μερικούς από τους αγαπημένους μας ήρωες. Από όσο γνωρίζω ο συγγραφέας είχε σκοπό να γράψει και άλλα τέτοια μικρότερα βιβλία που θα έδειχναν μερικές ακόμα πτυχές της ιστορίας αλλά δυστυχώς η αρρώστια τον πρόλαβε και στερηθήκαμε από μία σειρά από τέτοια μικρά αριστουργήματα που θα μεγάλωναν λίγο περισσότερο την επική κλίμακα του έργου του. Ο τροχός, όμως, γυρίζει όπως θέλει και τελικά άφησε να γραφτεί μόνο αυτό, οπότε ας το διαβάσουμε και ας το απολαύσουμε χωρίς να σκεφτόμαστε τίποτα άλλο.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9755872940015245643" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1510794295" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1510794295" />
    <a title="Sarah" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3344685-sarah"><img alt="Sarah" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1388694025p2/3344685.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1510794295?book_show_action=true">Jan 15, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sarah" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sarah" href="/user/show/3344685-sarah">Sarah</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780356504759" href="/book/show/25371657-new-spring">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3344685-sarah?shelf=read-in-2016">read-in-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3344685-sarah?shelf=books-i-own-kindle">books-i-own-kindle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3344685-sarah?shelf=buddy-read">buddy-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1510794295" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12800441564350650741"><b>This book is currently Tor's ebook of the month and you can download a copy for free from their website here: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='https://ebookclub.tor.com/'>https://ebookclub.tor.com/</a><br/>It's only available until 11:59 PM ET on September 20th 2019 so grab it quick if you want it!</b><br/><br/><b>New Spring</b> is technically a prequel to the Wheel of Time series (it's about events that occurred approximately 20 years before <b>The Eye of the World</b>) but I was advised to read it after book 10, <b>Crossroads of Twilight</b>, to avoid accidental spoilers. I'm not sure there were </span>
  <span id="freeText12800441564350650741" style="display:none"><b>This book is currently Tor's ebook of the month and you can download a copy for free from their website here: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://ebookclub.tor.com/">https://ebookclub.tor.com/</a><br />It's only available until 11:59 PM ET on September 20th 2019 so grab it quick if you want it!</b><br /><br /><b>New Spring</b> is technically a prequel to the Wheel of Time series (it's about events that occurred approximately 20 years before <b>The Eye of the World</b>) but I was advised to read it after book 10, <b>Crossroads of Twilight</b>, to avoid accidental spoilers. I'm not sure there were any major spoilers hidden in here but it definitely gives you an idea about which of the Aes Sedai can and can't be trusted so I can see why I was told to hold off on reading it until this point in the series.<br /><br />I'm really torn about how to rate this book, yes it was interesting to see how Moiraine and Siuan got involved in the search for the Dragon Reborn and I liked seeing a younger version of Lan but I'm not sure this actually gave us any new information that we haven't already discovered throughout the rest of the series. There weren't any major new revelations and it's hard to build tension in a story when you already know the outcome of events that follow on from it.<br /><br />It's also hard to be happy when you see how horrible one of your favourite characters used to be when they were a new Aes Sedai. I've always loved Moiraine, she is manipulative and she keeps far too many secrets but she's an interesting character and I always felt that she's trying to do the best for the people around her. Young Moiraine isn't a nice girl though, she's just as manipulative but she also has a vicious streak and the way she treated Lan was absolutely appalling. He's not the only person she made to suffer but because I'm so attached to his character I felt really bad for him. I just lost respect for Moiraine because she's so petty and willing to act as judge, jury and executioner for people she's barely met.<br /><br />It didn't help that we also got to meet Lan's carneira Lady Edeyn and once again a woman in the Wheel of Time series is a nasty piece of work. She took Lan's virginity when he was 15 (and she was in her 30s) and according to custom that gives her some kind of control over his life so she is now able to manipulate him back into her bed - somewhere he quite clearly didn't want to be! It's like the Tylin and Mat scenes all over again except Edeyn is plotting to marry Lan off to her daugher even while she's forcing him into her own bed. How did <b>Robert Jordan</b> consistently manage to create such horrible women and messed up relationships? I can't think of a single female character that I've liked throughout the entire series because he keeps turning them into whiny harpies or sex offenders and I'm so sick of that now. All the men are pushed around by nasty manipulative women and the Aes Sedai get away with murder because everyone else is terrified of them. At this point I'm half hoping Rand will go crazy and destroy the world!<br /><br />In spite of the issues mentioned and the fact that the plot moved at a snail like pace for at least the first two thirds of the book I still found myself enjoying it though. I don't know quite what that says about me but there you have it - I've obviously lost all sense of perspective when it comes to this series. I'll just say that I'm glad we're closing in on the end now, I almost wish I'd never started reading it but I'm really hoping that the last few books will be amazing enough to make me forget about the drudgery from the middle of the series.<br />________________<br /><br />Buddy read with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/topic/show/17825154-new-spring" rel="nofollow noopener">Buddies, Books &amp; Baubles</a> starting <b>26th October 2016</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="12800441564350650741" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_3194103931" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3194103931" />
    <a title="Eon ♒Windrunner♒  " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3481302-eon-windrunner"><img alt="Eon ♒Windrunner♒  " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1551272804p2/3481302.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3194103931?book_show_action=true">Jul 17, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Eon ♒Windrunner♒  " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Eon ♒Windrunner♒  " href="/user/show/3481302-eon-windrunner">Eon ♒Windrunner♒  </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/8892653-new-spring">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3194103931" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14150026298121445377">3.5 stars<br/><br/><i><b>He is born again!” Gitara cried. “I feel him! The Dragon takes his first breath on the slope of Dragonmount! He is coming! He is coming! Light help us! Light help the world! He lies in the snow and cries like the thunder! He burns like the sun!”</b><br/><br/>New Spring is a prequel novella for The Wheel of Time and even though I have read the main series a couple of times, I have never read this one. This time around I decided that I would start with the prequel as the blurb mentions that part of the</i></span>
  <span id="freeText14150026298121445377" style="display:none">3.5 stars<br /><br /><i><b>He is born again!” Gitara cried. “I feel him! The Dragon takes his first breath on the slope of Dragonmount! He is coming! He is coming! Light help us! Light help the world! He lies in the snow and cries like the thunder! He burns like the sun!”</b><br /><br />New Spring is a prequel novella for The Wheel of Time and even though I have read the main series a couple of times, I have never read this one. This time around I decided that I would start with the prequel as the blurb mentions that part of the story is of how Moiraine and Lan first met. It didn’t hurt either that Jason Chan’s cover art depicting Lan &amp; Moiraine is absolutely gorgeous, but once I started reading I was overjoyed to be back in this world and to have an unknown (to me) Robert Jordan story to experience.<br /><br />The book, for the most part, has us following a young Moiraine &amp; Siuane as Accepted, training in the White Tower to become Aes Sedai. Perchance they are present when a Sister has a foretelling of the imminent birth of the Dragon on the slopes of Dragonmount and they secretly endeavour to be the ones to find the boy. The rest of the story is focused on when &amp; how Lan &amp; Moiraine meet for the first time, and how they come to be the team we know.<br /><br /><i><b>We win this battle, or the world dies.</b><br /><br /><u>Highlights:</u><br />• Seeing young Moiriane &amp; Siuan and realising how much they have matured and become world-wise and better people in the main series. <br />• Everything al’Lan Mandragoran. Tai'shar Malkier!<br /><br /><i><b>“To stand against the Shadow so long as iron is hard and stone abides. To defend the Malkieri while one drop of blood remains. To avenge what cannot be defended.” </b><br /><br />• Aes Sedai testing.<br />• Black Ajah left, right and centre!!!<br /><br /><u>Lowlights:</u><br />• Seeing young Moiriane &amp; Siuan and realising how immature, naive and inconsiderate their young selves still are. <br />• Ok, there is some really messed up, weird shit going on with Borderland romance customs and I have blocked it out. <br />• Moiraine using questionable weaves and making really questionable choices.<br />• Moiraine being horrible to Lan. Repeatedly. Putting this one down to youth as she is not this way later on. You are forewarned.<br /><br />I had a great time reading this but there are definitely some issues that may affect your future views on some of the characters. I’m choosing to focus on the good stuff that I am happy I got to read, and while this is nowhere close the best WoT has to offer, I loved being given a peek into the past of these important characters.<br /><br /></i></i></i></span>
  <a data-text-id="14150026298121445377" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
