<div id="review_3213731368" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3213731368" />
    <a title="Mike&#39;s Book Reviews" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/59173659-mike-s-book-reviews"><img alt="Mike&#39;s Book Reviews" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1599347737p2/59173659.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3213731368?book_show_action=true">Mar 03, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mike&#39;s Book Reviews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mike&#39;s Book Reviews" href="/user/show/59173659-mike-s-book-reviews">Mike&#39;s Book Reviews</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780765306296" href="/book/show/1001544.New_Spring">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3213731368" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7937736254523288563">Full Video Review Here: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='https://youtu.be/3OO9C1752BI'>https://youtu.be/3OO9C1752BI</a><br/><br/>There has been a lot of debate from "Wheelies" on exactly when I should have read New Spring, but I decided after Crossroads of Twilight was the best time before beginning the final arc in this series. All I knew was that I didn't want to read it at the end because I want A Memory of Light to be my final impression of this world.<br/><br/>This is the story of not only how Lan became Moiraine's Warder, but also chronicles her time as Accepted and the orig</span>
  <span id="freeText7937736254523288563" style="display:none">Full Video Review Here: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://youtu.be/3OO9C1752BI">https://youtu.be/3OO9C1752BI</a><br /><br />There has been a lot of debate from "Wheelies" on exactly when I should have read New Spring, but I decided after Crossroads of Twilight was the best time before beginning the final arc in this series. All I knew was that I didn't want to read it at the end because I want A Memory of Light to be my final impression of this world.<br /><br />This is the story of not only how Lan became Moiraine's Warder, but also chronicles her time as Accepted and the origins of her search to find the Dragon Reborn. There's the usual poilitcs of the White Tower, plenty of familiar faces and names, as well as the usually Robert Jordan third act that knocks your socks off.<br /><br />The good is that if you are one of those, such as myself, that has been begging for Lan to have a bigger role in the main series this will give you your fix. Lan has his own adventure before eventually crossing paths with Moiraine and we get to see him in action in ways the regular series hasn't shown me yet (I'm currently reading book #12).<br /><br />The not so good is the usual fluff from Mr. Jordan. Too much time is spent on dress shopping and making bank deposits but at 334 pages, this is pretty streamlined for Jordan and it's a welcome pace.<br /><br />In the end, it's worth reading if you want to know how and why Lan and Moiraine were a well-oiled unit at the beginning of the main series. But it's nothing that is going to change the way you view the world or its characters.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7937736254523288563" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1959864751" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1959864751" />
    <a title="Andreas" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/20379307-andreas"><img alt="Andreas" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1512938270p2/20379307.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1959864751?book_show_action=true">Apr 04, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Andreas" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Andreas" href="/user/show/20379307-andreas">Andreas</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20379307-andreas?shelf=2017">2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20379307-andreas?shelf=owned">owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20379307-andreas?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20379307-andreas?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1959864751" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10534316985056666605">This novel is the prequel to the Wheel of Time series. It describes the coming-of-age of Moiraine Damodred and Siuan Sanche as Aes Sedai and how Moiraine and how al'Lan Mandragoran came to be Moiraine's Warder.<br/><br/>I've read the last book of the Wheel of Time, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7743175.A_Memory_of_Light__Wheel_of_Time___14_' title='A Memory of Light (Wheel of Time, #14) by Robert Jordan' rel='nofollow noopener'>A Memory of Light</a>, back in January 2013. This was 22 years after I read the first novel in the series. Quite a journey for 14 novels, hum? Though I consider myself a light fan of this series, I never have read the short story New Spring when Ro</span>
  <span id="freeText10534316985056666605" style="display:none">This novel is the prequel to the Wheel of Time series. It describes the coming-of-age of Moiraine Damodred and Siuan Sanche as Aes Sedai and how Moiraine and how al'Lan Mandragoran came to be Moiraine's Warder.<br /><br />I've read the last book of the Wheel of Time, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7743175.A_Memory_of_Light__Wheel_of_Time___14_" title="A Memory of Light (Wheel of Time, #14) by Robert Jordan" rel="nofollow noopener">A Memory of Light</a>, back in January 2013. This was 22 years after I read the first novel in the series. Quite a journey for 14 novels, hum? Though I consider myself a light fan of this series, I never have read the short story New Spring when Robert Silverberg collected a few novellas in his anthology <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/77232.Legends" title="Legends by Robert Silverberg" rel="nofollow noopener">Legends</a> in 1998.<br />New Spring is the extended version of the novella. It was published somewhere between book 10 (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/113435.Crossroads_of_Twilight__Wheel_of_Time___10_" title="Crossroads of Twilight (Wheel of Time, #10) by Robert Jordan" rel="nofollow noopener">Crossroads of Twilight</a>) and 11 (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13888.Knife_of_Dreams__Wheel_of_Time___11_" title="Knife of Dreams (Wheel of Time, #11) by Robert Jordan" rel="nofollow noopener">Knife of Dreams</a>) which were the last two books in the series to appear while Jordan was alife. <br /><br />Reading this short novel is, I assume, a journey back home for me. To al'Lan Mandragoran, Lord of the Lakes, Lord of the Seven Towers, True Blade of Malkier, Defender of the Wall of First Fires, Bearer of the Sword of the Thousand Lakes, Dai Shan <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[, and also known as the Aan'allein to the Aiel <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. I think this was the character which most of all drew me into the series, as I thought of him as Aragorn from LotR, as Allanon from Shannara, or maybe as Lancelot from the Arthurian saga. <br />Oh joy, when I read the first chapter with exactly this protagonist going for the Aiel. <br />But also to the Aes Sedai of Tar Valon, the Dragonmount, to Moiraine Damodred of the House of Cairhien. <br />Does this sound sesquipedalian, maybe a touch too epic? Well, welcome to the prequel of the Wheel of Time, I say :)<br /><br />Then we meet Moiraine Damodred, still fresh and young, shivering in the cold, and obviously not yet an Aes Sedai. Later Amyrlin Siuan Sanche is on her side serving the Amyrlin and the Keeper in a most prominent situation, the foretelling of the Dragon Reborn.<br />More interesting to me was the battle in the background, the last and decisive battle of the Aiel war, the so called "Battle of the Shining Walls" - the whole war being a revenge act for the "treekillers". That was where Tham al'Thor found his son, the series's main protagonist Rand al'Thor - a fact which isn't mentioned in the novel at all.<br /><br />In between a tiny bit of action, lots of shuffling around of Aes Sedaian coming-of-age and very many names which are mostly known from the series and are mainly targeted to fans of the series. <br />For example, don't miss out Elyas Machera, a wolf brother who had a prominent role in the first book of the series and is still a Warder here. Also, enter Cadsuane :)<br /><br />The last part had a good piece of action, something that I missed a little bit in the previous 2/3; magic fight, sword fight, word fight, everything. <br />Moiraine's naivety with top secrets of the White Tower <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[e.g. talking about the Black Ajah in public <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> felt exaggerated.<br /><br />Lan's willingness to be bound came too sudden for me. Previously he was all like "never work with Aes Sedai, they might bind you", then one long afternoon and a small talk and he acknowledged without really knowing how that would work out.<br /><br />I gave the novel 4 stars. 3 for quality, plus one for me as a fan of the series. I wouldn't recommend it to readers who don't know the series because of all the name dropping. I also don't know at what stage in reading I'd recommend it - certainly not after book one, because narration is uncertain and your view as a reader would change too much if read too early. But maybe a few books later in the series when you've got a better understanding about the setting in general. Best might be in publication order, i.e. after <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/113435.Crossroads_of_Twilight__Wheel_of_Time___10_" title="Crossroads of Twilight (Wheel of Time, #10) by Robert Jordan" rel="nofollow noopener">Crossroads of Twilight</a>. Or like me after reading the whole thingy. When you want to re-read the whole series, it would be a good idea to start with New Spring.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10534316985056666605" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1618709721?book_show_action=true">Apr 04, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="C.P. Cabaniss" class="user" itemprop="url" name="C.P. Cabaniss" href="/user/show/9656259-c-p-cabaniss">C.P. Cabaniss</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780765306296" href="/book/show/1001544.New_Spring">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9656259-c-p-cabaniss?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9656259-c-p-cabaniss?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1618709721" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15801152854194613575">Maybe 2.5 stars. I'm not entirely sure. <br/><br/>This started out very promising. Moiraine and Siuan were young and learning about the Dragon Reborn. It had all the makings of a fascinating story. And then it fell flat. <br/><br/>The first couple of chapters were exciting and had me really invested. Then the story became about Moiraine and Siuan in the Tower, and while I found some of this interesting, I didn't find it all that relevant. There was enough of Tower politics given in the main series, we didn't need q</span>
  <span id="freeText15801152854194613575" style="display:none">Maybe 2.5 stars. I'm not entirely sure. <br /><br />This started out very promising. Moiraine and Siuan were young and learning about the Dragon Reborn. It had all the makings of a fascinating story. And then it fell flat. <br /><br />The first couple of chapters were exciting and had me really invested. Then the story became about Moiraine and Siuan in the Tower, and while I found some of this interesting, I didn't find it all that relevant. There was enough of Tower politics given in the main series, we didn't need quite so much detail here. Still, it did have its interesting moments and it was nice to see all the young versions of the characters, already knowing what they would become later on. <br /><br />Lan was one of my favorite characters through the series, so I was looking forward to learning more about him. And this was probably one of the more satisfying things about this book. We did learn a little more about his heritage and the war he was always wanting to fight. I would have liked more focus on him and less on Moiraine, honestly. But even he had his down moments. I was not a fan of the Edeyn portions of the story. Luckily there was not much focus there, but he was stupid and she really weirded me out. I thought Tylin was bad, but this was a hundred times worse. <br /><br />The most disappointing thing about this book was Moiraine. Once outside the Tower she became insufferable. I never loved her in the main series, but I didn't expect her to be quite so cruel. She was constantly punishing people for things she had no right to punish them for, she tortured Lan (quite literally), and never seemed to learn a thing. All of the idiotic and outright cruel things she did just seemed to make her worse. It was quite excruciating, really. <br /><br />I'm not sure this review makes much sense. There were parts of this that were so promising and good. But overall these little things added up to something too big to ignore. I am glad I read this, however. <br /><br />And here ends my journey through The Wheel of Time. It's hard to believe that I've been reading this series for over a year. And now I'm finished. It will be odd not to have another one to pick up. <br /><br />An interesting prequel but I don't think it's necessary to read it. And if you do read it, I think reading after the 14 main books makes the most sense. I don't think I would have gotten as much from the story had I read it earlier in the sequence.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15801152854194613575" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer4836241739507407064">Prequel 'New Spring', a short book written after book ten in the 'Wheel of Time' series, is the story of how Moiraine Damodred and Siuan Sanche became Aes Sedai. It also relates how Lan Mandragoran met Moiraine. It explains why they decided to find the 'Dragon Reborn.' I have finished the entire series, and I can say reading this book out of order will not hurt a reader's enjoyment of the main series at all. It does fill in some history. However, the reader will not find this novel as exciting a</span>
  <span id="freeText4836241739507407064" style="display:none">Prequel 'New Spring', a short book written after book ten in the 'Wheel of Time' series, is the story of how Moiraine Damodred and Siuan Sanche became Aes Sedai. It also relates how Lan Mandragoran met Moiraine. It explains why they decided to find the 'Dragon Reborn.' I have finished the entire series, and I can say reading this book out of order will not hurt a reader's enjoyment of the main series at all. It does fill in some history. However, the reader will not find this novel as exciting as the official first book, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/34897.The_Dragon_Reborn__Wheel_of_Time___3_" title="The Dragon Reborn (Wheel of Time, #3) by Robert Jordan" rel="nofollow noopener">The Dragon Reborn</a>. In all honesty, if I had read 'New Spring' first, I may have not continued with the series. Reading it out of order as I did, though, I liked it and it was interesting as a backstory.</span>

I first read it in Legends, then I read the hardcover upon its release. Now I listened to the audio version. Well presented. <br/><br/></span>

<div id="review_2318385158" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2318385158" />
    <a title="Ashley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1343864-ashley"><img alt="Ashley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1597876967p2/1343864.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2318385158?book_show_action=true">Mar 15, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ashley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ashley" href="/user/show/1343864-ashley">Ashley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1343864-ashley?shelf=shop-on-your-own-shelves-2018">shop-on-your-own-shelves-2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1343864-ashley?shelf=espionage">espionage</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1343864-ashley?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1343864-ashley?shelf=you-wrote-about-what-now">you-wrote-about-what-now</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2318385158" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17372079538255243148">Okay, so, two and a half star book, for me. I waffled between two and three stars for ages, but I'm going with two, I think, for a couple of reasons. One, what is the arc here? It's sort of Moiraine becoming a real Aes Sedai, but there isn't really any emotional development on her part. She is the same person before she passes the test for the shawl as she is after. I liked that person for the first half, then she did some questionable shit, and I stopped feeling so charitably towards her.<br/><br/>Plus, </span>
  <span id="freeText17372079538255243148" style="display:none">Okay, so, two and a half star book, for me. I waffled between two and three stars for ages, but I'm going with two, I think, for a couple of reasons. One, what is the arc here? It's sort of Moiraine becoming a real Aes Sedai, but there isn't really any emotional development on her part. She is the same person before she passes the test for the shawl as she is after. I liked that person for the first half, then she did some questionable shit, and I stopped feeling so charitably towards her.<br /><br />Plus, there was all this gross sex stuff with Lan and the Malkieri that I just found really unappealing, and I don't care what Jordan was trying to do with it, gender roles reversing, blah blah blah, it just annoyed the hell out of me and me feel worse about everybody. Google "carneira" and "Wheel of Time" and see if it doesn't make all the blood vessels in your head explode. Yay, culturally sanctioned rape! Whoops, spoiler alert.<br /><br />So this book was totally billed as the story of how Moiraine and Lan met for the first time, and while that is *technically* a thing that happens in this book, it's certainly not the focus. Lan is barely in it, and Moiraine doesn't even leave the Tower until 60% of the way through. The book begins the day Rand is born, with the end of the Aiel War, and Moiraine and Siuan witnessing a sister having a Foretelling, that the Dragon Reborn is currently being born on the Dragonmount. They, along with the Amyrlin, are the only ones who know of the Foretelling, as the sister promptly dies immediately afterwards. <br /><br />The rest of the book features Moiraine and Siuan insinuating themselves into the hunt for the Dragon Reborn, which is undertaken in secrecy, but of course the Black Ajah gets wind of it, and Black Ajah fuckery abounds. Most of the book is taken up with Aes Sedai political maneuvering veiled in Jordan's typical manner. If that doesn't drive you absolutely bonkers, you might enjoy this book. It felt more behind the scenes than the Aes Sedai stuff normally does. Maybe Jordan felt he could go into a bit more detail since this was a prequel. (Do we never get to see any of our regular main characters pass the test and "officially" earn the shawl?)<br /><br />The book ends with Moiraine having left the White Tower and making Lan her Warder. (Which is another super annoying thing: Moiraine is a complete cow to Lan 100% of the time. Why did he agree to be her Warder. If she wanted a damn apology, she should have just fucking asked for one instead of sending plagues of bitey insects at him every night for a week. And talking about taming him all the time! UGH JUST TALK TO HIM LIKE HE IS A PERSON YOU VILE WOMAN. And Lan! You stupid fucker! If she is insulting you, OBVIOUSLY NOT KNOWING SHE IS DOING SO, then fucking tell her so she can stop! YOU UTTER MOO-RONS.) I used to like both of them!<br /><br />Overall, mixed bag of a book. I love Siuan. I loved the first half with her friendship with Moiraine, which felt real to me. I liked seeing all the behind the scenes White Tower stuff, and how they reacted to the Foretelling. I did NOT like the middle part that dragged a bunch and nothing happened. Did not like Moiraine being a huge asshole (leaving a woman to be gang-raped is not justice, Moiraine, even if she meant the recipient of it to be you). I did not like all the gross rapey shit with Lan. I did not like how they met or that they are now stuck with each other. Bleh. Disappointing. <br /><br />(But still, a vast improvement over the last two books of the series where NOTHING HAPPENED. At least lots of stuff happened here. And it was half the size!)<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17372079538255243148" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2291681870" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2291681870" />
    <a title="YouKneeK" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25923230-youkneek"><img alt="YouKneeK" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1386369592p2/25923230.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2291681870?book_show_action=true">Feb 14, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="YouKneeK" class="user" itemprop="url" name="YouKneeK" href="/user/show/25923230-youkneek">YouKneeK</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/8892653-new-spring">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25923230-youkneek?shelf=completed-series">completed-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25923230-youkneek?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2291681870" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17188702510965971916"><i>New Spring</i> is a prequel novel in the <i>Wheel of Time</i> series. It fleshes out several bits of back story that are provided throughout the first several books. I think I’m just going to stop there as far as explaining what it’s about. People familiar with the series can probably guess part of it just from looking at the cover, at least the cover for my edition, but the book was about a lot more than that and (slight spoiler) <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[the scene on the cover was actually one of the last scenes in</span></span>
  <span id="freeText17188702510965971916" style="display:none"><i>New Spring</i> is a prequel novel in the <i>Wheel of Time</i> series. It fleshes out several bits of back story that are provided throughout the first several books. I think I’m just going to stop there as far as explaining what it’s about. People familiar with the series can probably guess part of it just from looking at the cover, at least the cover for my edition, but the book was about a lot more than that and (slight spoiler) <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[the scene on the cover was actually one of the last scenes in the book <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. <br /><br />Despite knowing the major events that would take place based on what had already been revealed in the main books, I really enjoyed this. It was fun to see all of the details fleshed out. I chose to read it in publication order, which was between books 10 and 11. To my mind, things seem to fit more smoothly if I read them in the order the author created them. I think most people recommend waiting until at least after book 5 to read this, and that does make sense. Although it wouldn’t really spoil anything too major, it would take away the ambiguity of some of the characters throughout the main books. I also think this book has more meaning when you already know the bits of backstory already revealed.<br /><br />I have a few more spoiler-ish comments in the tags below. Please note that there are some spoilers up through book 10 in the series.<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I really enjoyed seeing Moiraine and Siuan in their early days as close friends. In the main books we’ve been told they were friends, and there was certainly some evidence of that, but we never really saw its depth or its history. I also enjoyed seeing their relationships with some of the other members of the White Tower. It was interesting that apparently Elaida was trying to help them in her own twisted way, at least until she believed they betrayed her. It was great to finally see exactly what’s involved in being raised from Accepted to Aes Sedai, and I liked learning more about some of their rules and customs. Lan’s part of the story was slightly less interesting by comparison, but it was much shorter and I did still enjoy it. I also enjoyed seeing how Moiraine and Lan met, and learning exactly how and why he became her warder.<br /><br />In at least the first couple WoT books, I had always felt like there was a tiny bit of ambiguity about Moiraine. I was pretty sure she was on the side of good, but her motives were always at least a little bit in question in my mind. The same was true of Siuan Sanche when she was first introduced. This book completely removes all ambiguity about those two characters and their motives, so that’s one reason I’m glad I didn’t read it in chronological order.<br /><br />Another ambiguous character in this book is Cadsuane. She remains ambiguous throughout her few appearances and mentions, and Moiraine ends up believing she’s probably part of the Black Ajah. Cadsuane has been a very ambiguous character in the main books also, although I’ve finally decided she’s probably one of the good ones. Spending some time in her POV has helped. However, we already know of at least one member of the Black Ajah who is supporting Rand because she believes he has to live until the final battle so he can be defeated. It’s possible Cadsuane also has ulterior motives for the choices she’s made that haven’t been fully revealed, so I could still be wrong about her. For now, though, I’m sticking with my belief that she’s not evil. I think, if I’d read <i>New Spring</i> before coming to my own conclusions about her, I would have been heavily influenced by Moiraine’s suspicions about her. I’m glad I had the chance to form my own opinion, even if it proves to be wrong. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>
  <a data-text-id="17188702510965971916" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3195175651" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3195175651" />
    <a title="Sud666" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/36890366-sud666"><img alt="Sud666" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1418437112p2/36890366.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3195175651?book_show_action=true">Mar 23, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sud666" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sud666" href="/user/show/36890366-sud666">Sud666</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780765345455" href="/book/show/372306.New_Spring">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36890366-sud666?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3195175651" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15913559481814015049">The New Spring is a prequel to the massive Wheel of Time series. I've already read the first and second book in the series, so I thought I may as well stick this prequel in due to chronological order. I'm glad I did. <br/><br/>The story revolves around the story of Moiraine Damodred and Siuan Sanche, both young Accepted who seek to become Aes Sedai sisters. It is also the story of Lan the Warder and how he became a Warder and met Moiraine.<br/><br/>The book is a great look into the training required to become an Ae</span>
  <span id="freeText15913559481814015049" style="display:none">The New Spring is a prequel to the massive Wheel of Time series. I've already read the first and second book in the series, so I thought I may as well stick this prequel in due to chronological order. I'm glad I did. <br /><br />The story revolves around the story of Moiraine Damodred and Siuan Sanche, both young Accepted who seek to become Aes Sedai sisters. It is also the story of Lan the Warder and how he became a Warder and met Moiraine.<br /><br />The book is a great look into the training required to become an Aes Sedai. The two main characters work their way from Accepted towards taking the Test, all with the backdrop of the possible rebirth of the Dragon. I enjoyed the look into the Aes Sedai, as well as gaining an understanding of Lan's background.<br /><br />A great story for any fan of the series and a good prequel. If there is only one complaint I have, it's a complaint I've pointed out in the other books as well, it is the sometimes irritating style he describes sword combat forms. I can guess, due to my extensive martial arts background some of what he means, but seriously? What does "Lotus Petal lands on Teacup" and "Butterfly on LSD" really do to describe the combat? Some of the forms make intuitive sense, but others are downright bizarre. Small bitch, I know, but it really spoils a good fight when the fighter ..." swiftly uses Pants With Button Fly Jeans and the men fell dead"..and that is supposed to suffice for the fight? Meh.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15913559481814015049" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('AHZ9AXEuKXgtlz7IGamp+u87AINylAm/zzBVtQzyRYVe6cO0nca+7uurJFkrOsr7cBD7wLZjrBSFLBiAIl7NHg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('L9DTsooDSQpzDG4mgdbKeLvYzwQGgsJz2MgSpnRKovBxT20HZuvenLUwdLezRal5JPM0R8J1Z9iS1F+TWuYqaw==')})
  }

      var newTip = new Tip($('bookCover_164672'), "\n\n  <h2><a class=\"readable bookTitle\" Out in the frontier lands known as the Roughs, they are crucial tools for the brave men and women attempting to establish order and justice.\n\nOne such is Waxillium Ladrian, a rare Twinborn, who can Push on metals with his Allomancy and use Feruchemy to become lighter or heavier at will. After twenty years in the Roughs, Wax has been forced by family tragedy to return to the metropolis of Elendel.       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/6252.Robert_Jordan">About Robert Jordan</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/6252.Robert_Jordan">Robert Jordan
</a></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer15983283822548051455"><i>Librarian Note: There is more than one author in the Goodreads database with this name.</i><br/><br/>Robert Jordan was the pen name of James Oliver Rigney, Jr., under which he was best known as the author of the bestselling The Wheel of Time fantasy series. He also wrote under the names <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/108933.Reagan_O_Neal' rel='nofollow noopener'>Reagan O'Neal</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/943931.Jackson_O_Reilly' title='Jackson O'Reilly' rel='nofollow noopener'>Jackson O'Reilly</a>.<br/><br/>Jordan was born in Charleston, South Carolina. He served two tours in Vietnam (from 1968 to</span>
  <span id="freeText15983283822548051455" style="display:none"><i>Librarian Note: There is more than one author in the Goodreads database with this name.</i><br /><br />Robert Jordan was the pen name of James Oliver Rigney, Jr., under which he was best known as the author of the bestselling The Wheel of Time fantasy series. He also wrote under the names <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/108933.Reagan_O_Neal" rel="nofollow noopener">Reagan O'Neal</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/943931.Jackson_O_Reilly" title="Jackson O'Reilly" rel="nofollow noopener">Jackson O'Reilly</a>.<br /><br />Jordan was born in Charleston, South Carolina. He served two tours in Vietnam (from 1968 to 1970) with the United States Army as a helicopter gunner. He was awarded the Distinguished Flying Cross with bronze oak leaf cluster, the Bronze Star with "V" and bronze oak leaf cluster, and two Vietnamese Gallantry Crosses with palm. After returning from Vietnam he attended The Citadel where he received an undergraduate degree in physics. After graduating he was employed by the United States Navy as a nuclear engineer. He began writing in 1977. He was a history buff and enjoyed hunting, fishing, sailing, poker, chess, pool, and pipe collecting. <br /><br />He described himself as a "High Church" Episcopalian and received communion more than once a week. He lived with his wife Harriet McDougal, who works as a book editor (currently with Tor Books; she was also Jordan's editor) in a house built in 1797. <br /><br />Responding to queries on the similarity of some of the concepts in his Wheel of Time books with Freemasonry concepts, Jordan admitted that he was a Freemason. However, "like his father and grandfather," he preferred not to advertise, possibly because of the negative propaganda against Freemasonry. In his own words, "no man in this country should feel in danger because of his beliefs."<br /><br />On March 23, 2006, Jordan disclosed in a statement that he had been diagnosed with cardiac amyloidosis, and that with treatment, his median life expectancy was four years, though he said he intended to beat the statistics. He later posted on his Dragonmount blog to encourage his fans not to worry about him and that he intended to have a long and fully creative life.<br /><br />He began chemotherapy treatment at Mayo Clinic in Rochester, Minnesota, in early April 2006. Jordan was enrolled in a study using the drug Revlimid just approved for multiple myeloma but not yet tested on primary amyloidosis.<br /><br />Jordan died at approximately 2:45 p.m. EDT on September 16, 2007, and a funeral service was held for him on Wednesday, September 19, 2007. Jordan was cremated and his ashes buried in the churchyard of St. James Church in Goose Creek, outside Charleston. </span>
  <a data-text-id="15983283822548051455" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
